<Review>I‚Äôm happy to start this review by saying this was the best massage I‚Äôve ever had.
No exaggeration.

I have had dozens of sports, deep tissue, Swedish, and myofascial release massages over the years.
The latter being the best experience thus far, but that was until visiting Malai Thai Massage.

I have never had a Thai Massage before. From my experience, it seemed like this modality utilizes more active techniques from the therapist than other more passive methods. And this I greatly appreciated.

Shifting my complements to the therapist, I‚Äôd like to give extraordinary praise to Ms. Lily and Ms. Apple.
Both therapist consistently checked on me during my sessions by asking if I was okay, or confirming if the pressure was fine. This attention to the client/guest can not be understated.

For those of you like myself that have had massages in the past where you ask the therapist to do something a certain way, but they just aren‚Äôt able to find that spot, adjust the pressure, or redirect there focus. It‚Äôs almost as if they‚Äôre just going through the motions instead of attending to the individuals specific needs.

But Ms. Lily and Ms. Apple were the opposite.
They not only checked on me, but actually listened to me and worked on the problem areas I mentioned.
And they did an awesome job.

And if it benefits you to know, at the time of this review, which is March 2021, they have a punch card to incentivize repeat visits. With the 10th session being half off.
Not bad.

And more on pricing.
I think there pricing is very fair and probably at a considerable discount compared to other private practice options.

As far as the studio.
It has a small foot print.
Even though they are located on the street, their signage is not very prominent, so be prepared to make a u-turn if you see the studio front as your passing it.

For the inside, it‚Äôs ambience is quiet, dimly lit, whispers of soft soothing music, and touches of Southeast Asia decor.

The only downside to the interior is that each massage table is only separated by curtains. So if your next to someone that is talkative or is sensitive to medium to firm pressure, you may hear them.
But from my multiple visits thus far, that has only be an annoyance once, and that was for a brief moment when a customer was talking loudly and being inconsiderate of his surroundings.

All in all, my experience was remarkable. Again, the best massage I‚Äôve ever had from the most attentive and involved therapist.

Thank you Malai Thai Massage, Ms. Lily, and Ms. Apple.

C- the neighboring stores and eateries are top notch. Awesome sushi right next door, the un-ironically Frank Sinatra-esque bar-slash-Italian food semi-dive joint is non stop fun and gossipy! < text>
AMMS is unique among martial arts schools.  They've taken the relatively young art of MMA and created a full curriculum with a ranking system that combines contemporary MMA with the doctrines of honor and respect typically associated with more traditional arts.   The training at AMMS is first rate and encompasses sport, athleticism, self defense, and personal growth. You can study stand-up (Western Boxing and Muay Thai), ground fighting (BJJ & Submission Wrestling), or both. If you are just looking for a tough workout, you won't be disappointed.  For those looking for a more serious pursuit of MMA or competition, AMMS offers that as well.

The students are welcoming and supportive and in a very short time I felt completely at home.  Many times, senior students would walk up and introduce themselves to me.  The facility is clean and well maintained.  They also have a great kids program.

Coach Jeremy, Kru Paulo, and Coach Akkim are all devoted instructors with years of both teaching and martial experience.  I took most of my classes with Coach Akkim and I must say that he is one of the finest coaches I have ever trained with.  He manages to adjust to the needs of each student (whether they are a black belt or it's their first day) and keep things challenging, but fun.  Old or young, Coach Akkim will help you improve.  My Boxing and Muay Thai improved in just a few short months.

For me, when training there are always good days and not so good days.  Days when I feel really on top and other days when I feel like I have two left-feet (which is funny cause I am left-handed), but even on my worst day I always left AMMS a little bit better because of the coaches and the other students.  I can't think of a better recommendation.</text>

<rate>5</rate><review>I recently joined AMMS. The school offers BJJ (Brazilian Jiu Jitsu), Muay Thai (Thai boxing), MMA and Close Quarter Contact classes. The main instructors are great, and definitely direct students looking to succeed within their system. [One of the cool things is that Khru Paolo Tocha (probably best known for his role in the movie Bloodsport).]

Classes involve technique, fitness and sparring. One definitely gets to practice the techniques and learn how well one is progressing in real scenarios.

Another cool note, recently the school opened the morning "Kick Fit" classes to any student of Muay Thai or BJJ at no extra cost.

Yes, this is a real school. And yes, this does sound like it would be one of the lame cardio-kickboxing classes from 'insert-a-gym'. It's definitely not. I started taking this in the morning to add to my exercise routine. The classes are great. They're brutal (if you really go for it), but they are great. Lots of plyometrics, Lots of cardio sprints.

All in all my first four months at the school have been great. I highly recommend checking it out. There are two locations: One in West Los Angeles (for the Westside) and one in Hawthorne (for the South Bay).</review>< pics>

Great Hawaiian fusion food!!! I really love their oatmeal fish combo plate. It comes with fish, rice, mixed veggies and macaroni salad for less than 9$. They offer teriyaki beef & chicken, oatmeal shrimp just to name a few items. The oatmeal shrimp & fish are surprisingly not greasy even though they are deep fried.</Review>

< Review>
I would not recommend National Covers for a bimini top. The only positive thing I can say, is the product does appear to be well made. When ordering a custom bimini top, suppling correct measurements, boat type, frame size and style...you would expect a good fit. Not the case! Our top was made way too small. We ordered a top 96 x 97-103, the one they sent came 93 x 96.5. Contacted customer service, sent item back and they are telling us, it's because of our frame and that the measurements are correct. <userid>101038321108840259205</userid>< username>
Sexy Jeep</username>
<time>1616536208832<//time><Rate>3< /Rate>< Text>
The cover I ordered was a perfect fit with the advice of one of their sales reps to go a foot longer on the cover to accommodate the attached trolley motor I have.  The material on my cover was the next level down from the Sunbrella material (WindStorm), but it was good enough for my short term use and the description of the material held true to it's look and feel in person - it was very nice!  The elastic fit and markings to install (front vs. back) were great as well.  For someone looking for a cover for short term use, this is a better bang for your buck than Sunbrella for sure.  The included straps were nothing special, but they do the job and held the cover on firmly and securely for a 600 mile journey at highway speeds.

There were two issues with this purchase though: as described below:

1.  The "600D" storage bag that was supposed to come with it to store the cover was not in the box.  The website showed that even on my custom "foot longer cover" that it would still come with the storage bag, but it did not.  I still need to reach out to customer service about this to see if they can send me one free of charge.

2. Although the instructions for the cover warn you to make sure there are no sharp edges on your boat before installing the cover, I would say that is not good enough.  I made sure the prop from my trolley motor was taken off to prevent it from acting like a knife on the underside of the cover, I removed my gps/fish-finder leaving only the rounded mounts that stick up on the driver's side console, and even removed my rear mounted radio antenna - leaving only the small threaded nub where the antenna fastens back on.  The boat/cover seemed to be working fine on my 600 mile trip to North Carolina, but nearly 120 miles in when I stopped for gas, I saw that the cover had been ripped open in two places: the first being where the rounded plastic mounts were for the fish-finder, and the second being a tear above the nub where the antenna fastens.

I did not feel these surfaces were anywhere close to being abrasive, but I guess I was wrong.  When I got to my destination I had to use gorilla tape to try and seel the tears to prevent water from dripping in while it's in outside storage.  For $300+ dollars I am slightly disappointed due to this.  I would say that nothing rounded nor pointy, no matter if plastic, fiberglass, nor any other material should touch the underside of this WindStorm cover or it will easily tear.  I am going to have to see if maybe a seamstress can do some work to fix it for me.<//Text>

< Review>
I purchased an RV Cover for my 2016 33' Blackstone Travel Trailer.  Previously I had it parked at a storage facility under cover but it cost me $140 per month so I decided to squeeze it in at our home. It got extremely dirty in storage even though it was under cover. I ordered one to cover a 33' trailer and this cover fits really nicely and the quality is great. It even covers my Propane Tank cover which I didn't expect. It should pay for itself in a couple of months. I was a little disappointed that they didn't include the gutter covers (that was an additional cost) so I improvised and created some covers from some foam wrap.

I installed it with the help of another person by starting on the roof and working my way down. It would be pretty difficult with one person. It went on pretty easily once we had it oriented correctly. We will need to get into the trailer periodically so I will need to peel back the cover (not remove it) and secure it for up to a week at a time to allow guests access and to move the slides out and back in so we'll see how the zippered sections hold up. It hasn't weathered a winter yet so I gave a 4 star. I'm reserving final judgment until I see how it holds up to the seasons.</Review>

<Date>1570729431961<//Date><rating>5</rating><review>I needed a decent RV cover for my new travel trailer.
Living in Canada, the winters can be harsh and I shuddered at the thought that my trailer would be encrusted with ice and snow without protection, especially the vulnerable bits on the roof (air conditioner, refrigerator vent, skylight and ceiling fan cover).
The thought of a standard tarp crossed my mind, but these typically trap moisture and may not stay in place all that easily.
The National Covers option, while a bit more expensive, does seem to provide good protection from the elements as well as venting to permit airflow and no trapped moisture.
The zippered flaps on the door side are a bonus should access be necessary during the winter period.
The front and back have straps to snug the cover to my trailer, even around the ladder and bumper-mounted spare tire.
The front covers my battery box (even though the batteries are stored elsewhere for the winter).
Finally there are three belly straps that keeps everything in place and the cover stays put even in stiff winds.
I quite like the product and it is a peace-of-mind item, that while not absolutely necessary, does help to protect my trailer during the period that I cannot use it.</review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNsExh8-nIzbf9byRZHiqqlnz21t69MHQNazA-2=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics>< Response>

<Rating>2</Rating>< text>
Looks like maybe I had bad luck here, but my experience wasn't great. I ordered a pontoon boat cover specifically for mooring. After looking at the website, I was concerned on the fit, so I called and was assured that the covers were sized appropriately for mooring or storage. When I received the cover and attempted to put it on, it was way too big, by several feet in the length and width directions. No big deal, we're all human, I'll return it.

Getting the return approved took around two weeks, and only occurred after I threatened to contest the purchase with my credit card company (verbally and via email). Once they received it, getting the return processed and my refund approved took another week and a half (the purchase was $470), and again only occurred after I told them I was going to contest the charge by close of business the last day.

Takeaway is: decent product, but beware of the returns process.</text>

My daughter uses the Club Car precedent to get around the campus of the school where she works.  Avoids all the parking issues. <Review>Recently purchased the Expedition 2 cover for our new Rockwood 35FT. Ultralight trailer and could not be more happy with. Cover fits and looks great. I have had to get access to the inside of the trailer and with the  way the side zippers are position it makes it super easy. FYI  One thing I found is that on the top of our trailer we have a Wi-Fi booster with 2 short rubber antennas sticking up. The weight of the cover it self will bend them over especially when pulling the cover on. <user_name>Trace Collier</user_name><date>1528730808888</date><Rating>1< /Rating><Review>Horrible.  Had to file a complaint with the Better Business Bureau, and dispute the charge on credit card with Visa.
The semi-custom cover I ordered didn't fit as it was large enough for a boat 3 feet longer than mine, even though I used National's custom ordering system for my particular boat. I  can never use this cover to trailer because the cover would beat the boat to death, but I can use it to cover the boat in the marina, so I'll get half the value as promised.  I intend to keep the cover, even though the price tag was high for something that doesn't work as advertised.
The engine cover was too small. The method they use to size these things is to ask how much horsepower an engine has.  That system doesn't work because all engine manufacturers have different sizes for their individual engines.  A 200 horsepower Mercury is not the same size as a 200 horsepower Evinrude.  National should ask what brand of engine
and the horsepower  instead, then an appropriately sized cover could have been made and sent.  Customer service was horrible, and I still don't have a suitable engine cover 4 weeks later.
I have had to file a complaint with the Better Business Bureau in California because I can't get National's customer service department to send me a cover that will fit my engine.  As the cover was included in the price, the engine cover was a fairly expensive part of the deal.  I can only describe National's customer service, and Nicole in particular, as being "snarky."  She was completely unhelpful, and seemed to have no interest in making this customer happy with his expensive purchase.  I didn't spend $700 with this company to purchase a giant hassle.  I only wanted a good quality boat and engine cover for my new boat.  Now, I fear, we will end up in small claims court because they refused to make the order correct and send an appropriate engine cover.  It seems absolutely crazy to me. What ever happened to companies putting a little effort into making  customers reasonably happy with purchases?
Beware that their "semi-custom" boat covers really don't fit, and their engine covers are too small for modern engines.  Also beware that you may have poor luck getting issues resolved because customer service is geared to taking orders, not solving problems after they have your money.  If my engine cover problem is resolved, I will be happy to post an update, but I think that would require involvement from a level higher than customer service at this point.  Never again!!!!!< /Review>< pics>

< text>
I just put my new Goldline cover on my 35 foot 5er last light. Took a little longer than usual because I had to unfold it, and refold so it would go on right. It seems to be a little more difficult to put on due to the elastic corners, but fits very nice once it's on. Appears to be much more durable than my old cover, but time will tell. Word of advice, cover the drain spouts with pipe insulator wrapped in all weather tape. That is what lead to the early demise of my old cover. The storage bag is nice for transporting when it's new, but there is no way I'll ever be able to get it back in there now. My camper is 3 years old and looks like the day I got it, because I have kept it covered. The Goldline cover is not cheap, but far less expensive than your RV, and I'm sure it will save you a lot of depreciation at resale.</text>
